出自tedxboston這個開放的演講中 , 理查德・雷斯尼克告訴我們基因測序是如何廉價並快速得顛覆醫療體制 。	in this open speech from tedxboston , richard resnick tells us how sequencing the genome is cheap and rapidly disrupting the health system .
dna , biotech , healthcare , science , technology	dna , biological , healthcare , apocalypse .
理查德・雷斯尼克:歡迎進入基因革命時代	richard resnick: welcome to the genome revolution .
女士們先生們 , 我向您展示人類基因組	ladies and gentlemen , i'll show you the human genome .
左上是一號染色體	on the left is number one chromosomes .
右下是性染色體	here's a sex chromosome .
女性有兩條那個大大的x染色體男性有個x當然 , 還有個小小的y	the woman has two big x chromosomes , and of course there's an x , and there's a little y .

這個統一模型推測出了這兩種新子對應的粒子它們應該和弱力很相似但是效果更弱	this unified model has speculated these two newly corresponding particles that should be similar to weak forces , but they're weaker .
現在可以在七維空間中旋轉這個載荷集同時考慮一下關於粒子的奇怪現象:在六維載荷空間中物質的第二代和第三代擁有和第一代物質相同的載荷	now you can rotate this charge in sevendimensional space , consider the weird phenomenon of particles: the second and third generation of matter in sixdimensional charges have the same charge as the first generation .
這些粒子透過對應的六個載荷無法一一識別	these particles can't identify through six charges of corresponding .
在標準載荷空間上他們會彼此疊加	they overlay each other in standard charge space .
然而在八維載荷空間中我們可以賦予每一個粒子唯一的新載荷	but in 8dimensional charge space , we can give each particles the only new charge .
然後在八維空間中旋轉看看整體的圖案是什麼樣的	and then it rotates in eightdimensional space to see what the overall pattern looks like .
這裡我們可以看到物質的第二代和第三代透過一種叫 " 三重性 " 對稱和第一代相關聯	here we see the second generation of matter and the third generation by relating to a symmetry called the symmetry and the first generation .
在八維中的這個特殊的載荷圖案是數學中最為漂亮的幾何結構之一	this particular charge pattern in eightdimensional dimension is one of the most beautiful geometric structures in mathematics .
這是最大的例外型李群e8的圖案	this is the largest exception of e8 .
李群是光滑曲線形的248維空間	the colony is the 248dimensional space of the smooth curve .
圖案的每一點都能這個極其複雜而又美麗的圖案中找到對稱點	every single point of this pattern can find a symmetrical symmetry in this extremely complicated and beautiful pattern .
e8中的一小部分可以用來描述愛因斯坦廣義相對論中用來解釋重力的扭曲時空	a tiny fraction of the e8 can be used to describe the relativity of gravity in einstein's general relativity .
這個幾何形狀和量子力學一起能夠以最小的尺度描述萬物之理	these geometry shapes and quantum mechanics can describe everything at the smallest scale .
而在八維載荷空間中的這個圖案顯得異常美麗它還囊括了上千種這些基本粒子之間可能的相互作用每一種作用只是這個複雜形狀的一個平面	and this particular pattern in eightdimensional charge space is remarkably beautiful , and it also includes thousands of possible interactions between these basic particles , each of which is just a flat aspect of this complex shape .
轉動它時可以看到包含其中的很多錯綜複雜的圖案	and when you rotate it , you can see a lot of these intricate patterns .
透過某種旋轉我們可以在八維空間沿一個對稱軸方向觀察這個圖案並且一次看盡所有粒子	and by spinning a certain kind of rotation , we can look at this pattern along a symmetrical axis and see all the particles at once .
這是個很美的結構和其他統一理論一樣我們可以看到在這個圖案中有一些空格需要新的粒子來填補	it's a beautiful structure , a theory of other unified theories , and we can see that there are some empty particles in this pattern that need new particles to fill .
在這有20個空格需要新粒子來填補其中兩個已有帕蒂和薩拉姆粒子填補	there are 20 blanks that require new particles to fill in , and two of them have patty and salam particles filling .

多數情況下 , 這些極具攻擊性的行為是直接針對相鄰社群中個體的	in most cases , these extremely aggressive behaviors are directly opposed to individuals in the neighborhood community .
這些攻擊大多是為了爭奪地盤	most of these attacks are trying to fight for the plate .
我覺得 , 與別的生物相比黑猩猩更有助於我們認識到 , 人類和動物王國裡的其他成員終歸併無明顯界限	i think it's more helpful to recognize that the rest of us and the other members of the chimpanzee are in the kingdom .
這種界限非常模糊 , 並且隨著我們更多的觀察會一直更加模糊下去	this boundary is very ambiguous , and as more of our observations have been blurred .
我1960年開始的研究一直持續到現在	my research started in 1960 , and it's still going on .
這些黑猩猩在野生環境過著複雜的社會生活最重要的是 , 他們幫助我們認識到 , 我們與形形色色的動物在地球上共處 , 我們是其中一部分不能與這些動物分割開來	the most important thing about these chimpanzees living in a wildlife environment is that they help us recognize that we share with the shaped animals on the planet , and we're partly not separated from these animals .
所以 , 發現黑猩猩和世界上其他眾多生物一樣失去聚居地 , 是很讓人難過的	so it's very sad to find that chimpanzees , like many other organisms in the world , are losing habitat .
這只是一張從空中拍的照片你可以看到森林覆蓋的gombe高地	this is just a photograph taken from the sky , and you can see the globe covered in the forest covered .
16年前 , 我走遍整個地區意識到在公園之外 , 這片森林在1960年時沿著tanganyika湖東岸綿延不絕小巧的、面積只有30平方英里的gombe國家公園就坐落在這裡那時一個問題進入我腦海	16 years ago , i went around the region and realized that , outside the park , the forest spreading along the east coast of tanyika lake banka lake in 1960 , with only 30 square miles of gombe national park .
" 我們怎麼能進而去試圖拯救這些出了名的黑猩猩 , 而住在國家公園周圍的人卻在為生存而掙扎 ? "	" how can we go in and try to save these famous chimpanzees , and the people around the park are struggling to survive ? "
那裡人口眾多 , 非單薄的土地所能承受	there's a lot of people , nonthinland .
隨著來自蒲隆地的難民湧入來自剛果的人跨湖過來 , 住在那裡的人數增加著	and with refugees from burundied , the congolese people came across the lakes , the number of people living there increased .
那些人非常窮無力從別的地方買吃的	those people are very , very poor to buy food from elsewhere .
一個計劃由此產生 , 我們稱之為 " 關愛 "	so one of the projects that we call " love . "
它用整體化的方式來改善住在湖周圍村子裡的人的生活	it's integrated to improve the lives of people living in the villages around the villages .
剛開始是小規模的 , 有12個村子 。 現在是24個	at first , there are 12 villages . it's 24 .
這裡沒有時間去深入介紹 , 不過該計劃包括象林木苗圃等事情 , 以及適於在山上這片目前嚴重剝蝕幾近沙漠的土地上耕種的方法	there's no time to go deep , but the project includes things like beds of wood for beds , and the methods of farming in the mountains that are seriously eroding the deserts .
控制、防止土地侵蝕的方法	control , prevent land eroding .
收回過度使用的農田的方法以便兩年內這些農田可以重新有收成	in two years , these farms can be recycled by overdose farms .
幫助村民從井裡取得淡水	help the villagers get freshwater from well .
或許建一些校舍	maybe some campus .
我認為最重要的是與小規模群體婦女合作給她們提供微型信用貸款的機會	and i think the most important thing is to work with smallscale groups of women to provide microcredit opportunities for them .
全世界的情況一樣 , 在所有貸款中我們收回了大約95%	and we recycled about 95 percent of all loans around the world .
使婦女能夠受教育後工作給女孩子提供獎學金 , 以便讓她們完成中學學業很清楚 , 世界各地婦女的教育程度提高了 , 家庭人口數目就會下降	it allowed women to be educated to work in scholarships to provide scholarships so that they could fulfill their middle school , and the education of women all over the world increases , family populations will decline .
我們提供計劃生育和艾滋病及其病毒方面的資訊	we provide information about fertility and aids and their viruses .
這項計劃實施之後自然保護方面發生了一些事情	and then there's something that's happening in the conservation of this project .
自然保護方面發生的事情是 , 住在這24個村子裡的農民並沒有把我們看成是跑來研究整個一夥兒猴子的一夥兒白人順便說一下 , 現在很多工作人員是坦尚尼亞人而當我們開始 " 關愛 " 計劃時進入村子的是一個坦尚尼亞小組	what's happening in the natural protection is that farmers who live in these 24 villages don't see us as a partner of the whole monkey , and by the way , a lot of workers are tanzanians , and when we start to look at the village , it's a tanzanian team .
和村民交談的是一個坦尚尼亞小組詢問村民對什麼感興趣	talking to the village is a tanzanian team , asking what interests the villagers .
他們對自然保護感興趣嗎 ? 一點也不	are they interested in the conservation of nature ?
他們對健康感興趣 , 他們對教育感興趣	they're interested in health , they're interested in education .
隨著時間推移 , 隨著他們境況開始改善他們開始不斷理解更多有關自然保護的必要性	over time , as they started to improve their situation , they began to understand more about the need for natural protection .
他們開始理解當山上較高位置的數被砍光以後可怕的土地侵蝕和泥流就來了	they began to understand that when the higher mountains were cut down , the terrible erosion and the mud came .
現在 , 我們正在開發所說的大gombe生態系統	now , we're developing what we call the biggest gmbe ecosystem .
這是一片國家公園以外的地區綿延包括了所有這些各種各樣剝蝕了的土地	this is a national park outside of the park , including all these different kinds of erosions of land .
由於這些村子生活標準高一些他們實際上同意把他們土地的10-20%放到高地一側以便當樹長回來時黑猩猩會再次擁有綠色走廊它們可以藉此穿行以便這是他們基因繁殖所必需的與國家公園外其它殘餘群體互動	and because of these villages , they actually agreed to put 10 to 20 percent of their land on one side so that chimpanzees return green corridors , they can wear it so that it's necessary to interact with the rest of the park .
所以 " 關愛 " 計劃成功了	so love is successful .
我們在非洲其它地區複製這項計劃在其它面臨極端人口壓力的荒野之地	we replicate this project in other parts of africa in other parts of africa , in the wilderness of extremely stressed populations .
但是 , 就像我們在ted開始的所有這幾天一直討論的非洲的問題是主要問題	but , as we've been talking about at ted , the problem of africa in africa in the last few days is the major problem .
那裡非常貧窮	it's very poor .
有大量的人生活在不那麼肥沃的土地上尤其當你把樹砍倒使得土壤裸露 , 任風侵蝕同時處於絕望的人砍倒越來越多的樹以便為他們自己和家人努力培育糧食這樣會發生什麼 ? 有些東西會開始犧牲讓步	there's a lot of people living on less fertile land , especially when you cut down the trees and make them naked , wind erode , and at the same time desperately , cut down more and more trees to grow food for themselves and their families , so what happens ? something starts sacrificing .
還有別的問題不僅在非洲而且是其它所有發展中世界 , 甚至是地球上所有地方我們在對我們的地球做什麼呢 ?	and there's another question that isn't just in africa , it's in all the developing world , it's even everywhere on the planet , what are we doing about our planet ?
著名科學家 , e.o.威爾遜說過 , 如果地球上每個人的生活標準都達到歐美平均水平我們就再需要三個地球	well , the famous scientist , e . o . wilson said that if every person on the planet has reached the average standard of life on earth , we'll need three planets .
今天他們說是四個 。 可我們沒那些個 , 我們只有一個	today they say four . but we don't have those . we have one .
發生了什麼 ? 我是說 , 這裡的問題是 , 我們在這裡或許可稱為地球上有史以來最有智慧的生命有著非凡的大腦能夠運用這些ted會議上闡述備至的這些技術但我們卻在毀壞著這個惟一的家園	what's going on ? i mean , the question here , is , we might call the most intelligent life on earth , with extraordinary brains that can use these ted conferences to illustrate these technologies , but we're destroying this homeland .
全球各地的原住民在做重要決定前都會坐到一起 , 然後問 " 這決定如何影響我們接下來的七代人 ? "	indigenous people around the globe sitting together before making important decisions , and asking , " how does this decision affect the next seven generations ? "
今天 , 重要決定我這裡不特別談非洲而是發達世界牽涉幾百萬美元以及以及幾百萬人的重要決定卻只是問 " 這會如何影響下次股東大會 ? "	today , it's important to determine me not to talk about africa , but to introduce the world for millions of dollars and millions of people , but to just ask , " how does this affect the next shareholders ? "
這些決定卻影響非洲	these decisions affect africa .
當我開始遊歷非洲談論黑猩猩面臨的問題及其日益消逝的森林我愈來愈意識到如此之多的非洲問題是如何與以前的殖民開發有關的	and as i started wandering around africa and talking about the problem of chimpanzees and the dying of forests , i became more and more aware of how so much of africa's problems are related to colonial development .
因此我開始在非洲之外旅行 , 在歐洲演講在美國演講 , 去亞洲	so i started traveling beyond africa , talking in europe , speaking in the united states , going to asia .
每一地都有這些糟糕的問題	everywhere has these bad problems .

我們呼吸的空氣經常毒害我們	the air we breathe is often poisoning us .
泥土毒害我們的食物	mud poisons our food .
水水也許是本世紀我們要面對的最要緊問題之一每一地 , 水都被農業、工業、家用化學制品所汙染全世界都還在噴這些製品似乎沒辦法從過去的經驗獲利	water may be one of the most important issues we face in this century , and every time water is contaminated by agriculture , industrial , home chemistry systems , and around the world it seems to be able to profit from the past .
紅樹被砍倒海嘯等影響日益加重	the red trees are being cut down the tsunami , and so on and so forth .
我們談過土壤侵蝕	we've talked about soil erosion .
我們不計後果地燒過化石燃料連同其它所謂溫室氣體導致了氣候變化	we've burned fossil fuels in the same way that it's called greenhouse gases lead to climate change .
終於 , 全世界的人都開始相信有什麼事發生了 , 我們的氣候不對勁兒了	and finally , people around the world are starting to believe what's happening , and our climate is not right .
全球氣候互相牽連	global climate connections .
最受不利影響的是窮人	the poorest influence is poor people .
已經受影響的是非洲	what's already influenced is africa .
在次撒哈拉非洲的許多地區 , 乾旱非常嚴重	in many parts of subsaharan africa , drought is very serious .
雨終於下起來時 , 又常常導致洪水及更多的不幸 , 貧窮、飢餓和疾病週而復始	when the rain comes down , it often leads to flooding and more unfortunately , poverty , hunger and disease weekly .
還有很多人住在土地供養不起的地區太窮 , 買不起食物因為全部土地都剝蝕了 , 所以也沒法離開	there's a lot of people who live in an incredibly poor areas , can't afford food , because all lands are eroding , so there's no way to leave .
於是有了沙漠化一點點漫延 , 漫延 , 漫延同時最後的樹也被砍倒	so , with desertification , a little bit of a romantic , a long way , and the last trees have been cut down .
這種事情不光在非洲遍佈全球	it's not just in africa .
所以我不覺得奇怪當我在世界各地旅行時碰到那麼多年輕人 , 他們看上去失去了希望	so i don't think it's odd that when i travel around the world , i meet so many young people who seem to have lost hope .
我們似乎已經失去了智慧 , 那種屬於原住民的智慧	we seem to have lost the wisdom of indigenous peoples .
我想問 , 這是為什麼 ?	i want to ask , why is that ?
你們覺得在這異常聰明的大腦ted技術作為例證的那種大腦和人的心臟之間會有某種隔絕嗎 ? 用非科學的術語來談談根據愛和同情 。 有隔絕嗎 ?	do you think there's some kind of an isolation between the brain and the heart of the brain and the heart of the brain , in the nonscientific term , to talk about love and compassion ?
這些年輕人 , 當我和他們講話時基本上他們要麼情緒低落 , 要麼無動於衷或者痛苦、憤怒他們或多或少說的是同一件事情 " 我們這麼感覺是因為我們覺得你們損害了我們的未來 , 並且我們對此無能為力 。 "	these young people , when i talk to them , they're basically emotionally low , they're either obsessive or pain or anger or they're more or less likely to say the same thing , " we feel it's because we think you've damaged our future , and we can't do it . "
我們確實已經毀壞了他們的未來	we've actually destroyed their future .
我有三個小孫子 , 每次看著他們我就想 , 從我像他們那麼大以來 , 我們是如何損害這個美麗的地球的我感覺到這種絕望	i have three little grandchildren , and every time i look at them , i think , from the size of them , how do we damage this beautiful earth , i feel despair ?
我們由此開展這項我們稱之為 " 根與芽 " 的計劃恰好始於這裡 , 坦尚尼亞現在已經傳播到世界上97個國家	so we started this project called roots and shoots , where tanzania has now spread to 97 countries around the world .
專案的名字是具有象徵意義的根造就堅實的基礎	the name of the project is a symbolic symbol of the roots of meaning .
芽看上去細小 , 在陽光照耀下卻可穿破磚牆	it looks tiny , and it shines , and it shines through the brick walls .
磚可以看成是我們給地球造成的環境的和社會的問題這是希望的訊息	bricks are the environmental and social issues that we're giving to the planet , and that's the message of hope .
世界各地成千上萬的年輕人可以取得突破 , 為了所有生物 , 讓這個世界更美好	hundreds of thousands of young people around the world have access to breakthroughs , for all organisms , to make the world a better place .
" 根與芽 " 的最重要訊息每一天 , 我們每一個人都在改變世界	the most important message of roots and shoots , every day , every single one of us is changing the world .
我們有一個選擇這屋子裡我們每一個人我們都有一個選擇 , 關於我們想做些什麼來改變世界	we have a choice in our house , and we all have a choice about what we want to do to change the world .
很窮的人沒有選擇我們要改變這些事以便窮人也有選擇	poor people don't have options to change these things so that poor people have choices .
" 根與芽 " 小組都選三個方案	roots and shoots teams select three solutions .
取決於成員年齡 , 所在國家在城市還是鄉下 , 來選不同的方案	depending on the adult age , in the country , in the country , in the country , in the country , in the country , to select different solutions .
基本上 , 我們現在的計劃從學前一直到大學愈來愈多的成人開始建立他們自己的 " 根與芽 " 小組	essentially , we've been planning to go from school to college , and more adults start building their own roots and shoots .
每個小組在彼此之間選擇三種不同的方案 , 來創造更加美好的世界承認所有這些不同問題是互相聯絡彼此影響的	each group chooses three different solutions between each other to create a better world acknowledging that all of these different problems are interconnected .
因此他們的方案之一將會幫助他們自己的人類社群	so one of their solutions will help their own human community .
然後 , 如果他們能幹 , 他們可以籌集資金幫助世界上其它地區的社群	and if they can do that , they can raise funding to help the community in other parts of the world .
他們的方案之一將會幫助動物不光是野生動物也包括家養動物	one of their solutions will help the animals , not just wildlife , but domestic animals .
他們的方案之一將會幫助我們共處的環境	one of their solutions will help us share the environment .
交織在所有這些方案中的訊息是學著與我們自己、家庭、社群和諧相處 , 包括國家之間 , 不同文化之間不同宗教信仰之間 , 以及我們和自然世界之間	the message in all of these programs is that we learn to harmonize ourselves , families , communities , including countries , between different cultures , between religious beliefs and our natural world .
我們需要自然世界我們不能繼續象現在這樣破壞世界了	we need the natural world , and we can't keep destroying the world right now .
我們只有一個地球	we only have one planet .
就在非洲這裡 , 僅僅選出一個或兩個 " 根與芽 " 小組正在實施的方案只要一個或兩個方案在坦尚尼亞、烏干達、肯亞、南非、剛果、布拉扎維、獅子山、喀麥隆以及別的團體 。 就象我說的 , 遍佈世界97個國家	right here in africa , just one or two roots and shoots groups are implementing just one or two programs in tanzania , uganda , kenya , south africa , congo , sierra leone and other groups , i mean , 97 countries across the world .
當然 , 他們種樹 , 他們種有機蔬菜	of course , they plant trees , they grow organic vegetables .
他們在難民營養小雞賣雞蛋得些微薄收入或只是把雞蛋給家人吃並覺得自豪和獲得權力因為他們自己種植蔬菜養殖小雞就不再無助 , 不再依賴他人	they sell chicken chickens in refugee nutrients , or just eat chicken eggs for their families and feel proud and authoritarian , because they grow their own vegetable chickens no longer helpful , no longer depend on others .
這個方案在烏干達實施了給予前童軍一些心理上的幫助	the solution was implemented in uganda with some psychological help to the children's army .
實施這些方案讓他們重塑自我	it's implementing these programs to reinvent themselves .
再一次 , 他們成為社會上的有用一員	again , they became a member of society .
我們也在監獄實施該計劃	we also implemented it in prison .
所以現在沒時間實施更多的 " 根與芽 " 計劃	so there's no time to implement more roots and shoots .
哦 , 他們也致力於艾滋病及其病毒方面的工作	oh , they also work on aids and their viruses .
那是 " 根與芽 " 計劃非常重要的組成部分由大孩子跟小孩子談話	that's the roots and shoots project , and it's a very important component of adults talking to kids .
還有無意懷孕及類似事情年輕人更願意聽別的孩子的 , 而不是成人的	there's unintentional pregnancy and young people who are willing to listen to other kids , not adults .
希望 。 我周遊世界被問及的就是這個問題 " 珍 , 你見過這麼多可怕的事情 , 你看著你的黑猩猩數量在減少 , 從世紀之交的大約一百萬到現在的不足15萬 。 那麼多其它動物也一樣	hopefully , what i've been asking around the world is the question , " jane , you've seen so many terrible things , and you're looking at your chimpanzees decreasing from about a million to 150 , 000 , so many other animals are also the same .
森林消失 , 過去是森林的地方變成沙漠	the forest disappears . it used to be the forest to be desert .
你真的有希望 ? " 嗯 , 有 。	you really have hope ? " hmm , yeah .
你不可能來參加象ted這樣的會議 , 卻不報希望 , 對吧 ?	you can't come to a ted conference without hope , right ?
當然 , 有希望 。 希望之一是這令人稱奇的人腦	of course , there's hope . hope is one of these amazing human brains .
我是說 , 想一想技術	i mean , think about technology .
我最後還是很激動 , 碰到人們談論堆肥廁所	i'm still very excited to meet people talking about composting toilets .

我們就把所有這些水衝下馬桶 , 這很可怕	we just rushed all of these water down the toilet , which is terrible .
然後談論了可再生能源 , 非常重要	and then we talked about renewable energy , very important .
我們為孩子關心過地球嗎 ?	do we care about the planet for our children ?
我們多少人有孩子或者孫子、侄子、外甥 ?	how many of us have children or grandchildren , nephews , nieces ?

從弗雷明翰研究中我們得知如果你有三個好朋友都肥胖你也有一半肥胖的可能 。	and from the fremmen study , we learned that if three good friends are obese , you have half obese possibilities .
所以如果你和不健康的人在一起隨時間推移會受到很大影響 。	so if you're with unhealthy people , you're going to have a huge impact over time .

練習專案通常在一月開始十月結束 。	practice projects usually end in january .
至於長壽 , 沒有藥片或其他什麼東西能在短期內奏效 。	for longevity , there's no pharmaceutical or anything else that works in the short run .
但當你想到你的朋友是長期的冒險活動時 , 因此 , 它是你為增加壽命和讓生命生機勃勃能夠做的最重要的事情謝謝	but when you think about your friends as a longterm adventure activity , so it's the most important thing you can do for increased lifespan and increasing your lifespan .
能導電的墨水、一<unk>開關就由透明變不透明的窗戶、能播放音樂的果凍--這些東西確實存在 。 catarinamota說:現在是時候嘗試他們了 。 mota將帶領我們認識這些新穎和神奇的材料 , 她說 , 弄清楚這些材料的神奇之處的最好方式就是用它們來做實驗 , 不斷嘗試並樂在其中 。	the mechanism of the electricity , the messibility of the switch , the freezing of transparency windows , the frozen of the music that actually exists . catarina mota says , it's time to try them . it's time for us to take us to know these novel and magical materials , and she says that the most wonderful way of using these materials is to try and experiment with it .
creativity , design , technology	there's no need for life .
catarinamota:玩轉智慧材料	catarina mota: playing intelligent materials .
我有一位葡萄牙朋友 , 其祖父用一輛腳踏車和一臺洗衣機改裝成一輛汽車供家人乘用 。	i have a portuguese friend whose grandfather used a bicycle and a washing machine to multiply a car .
他這樣做 , 一是因為他買不起車 , 但更重要的是因為他知道如何改裝汽車 。	he did this one because he couldn't afford a car , but more importantly , because he knew how to fix a car .
曾經 , 我們都懂得一些機械的工作原理 , 也知道它們是怎麼製造出來的 , 所以我們能夠自己製作和維修它們.或者至少基於我們的瞭解作出明智的購買決定 。	we used to understand some mechanical work principles and figure out how they were made , so we could make and repair them , or at least based on our understanding of making smart buying decisions .
但我們很多這些diy的實用性技能在20世紀的下半葉就流失了 。	but a lot of these diy's practical skills disappeared in the bottom half of the 20th century .
但是現在 , 製作者社群和開放資源模式正在把這些物品的工作原理和製造材料的知識帶回到我們的生活中 。 而且我相信我們需要把這些知識帶到下一個層面 , 也就是了解構成這些物品的元件 。	but now , the producer community and opensource models are bringing the knowledge of these objects to work and make materials back into our lives , and i believe we need to bring these knowledge to the next level , which is understanding the components of these objects .
我們很多人都知道 , 像紙和織物這樣的傳統材料是什麼做成的 , 以及它們是如何生產的 。	many of us know what traditional materials like paper and fabric are made of and how they produce .
但是現在我們有了一些令人驚歎的未來複合材料-如可以變形的塑膠、可以導電的油漆、可以變色的顏料和可以發光的織物 。	but now we have some amazing future complexing materials such as transformable plastic , conducive paint , colorful and glowable fabric .
下面讓我們來看一些新材料 。	so let's look at some new materials .
這種導電墨水可讓我們 , 拋棄傳統的印刷電路板或電線的方法而直接用導電墨水來畫電路板 。	this conductive ink allows us to throw away the traditional printing boards or wires , directly draw the circuit boards .
比如我手裡拿著的這個小裝置 , 是我們用導電墨水做成一個觸控性的感測器 , 一旦接觸人的皮膚 , 這個小燈就會亮起 。	so for example , this little device that i'm holding in my hand , is a touch sensor that we make a touchal sensor , and once the contact encounters the person's skin , it lights up .
導電墨水已經被藝術家們應用到創作中了 , 最新的進展表明我們很快就能把它應用在鐳射印表機和鐳射筆中.	conduct ink has been applied to artists , and the latest progress shows that we can apply it to a laser printer and a laser laser .
這是一張泡浸過無色光漫顆粒丙烯酸的紙.	this is a piece of paper that has been immersed by an incredible comic of light .
只浸過普通丙烯酸的紙只在其邊緣周圍有漫光現象 , 而這張浸過無色光漫顆粒丙烯酸的紙 , 當我們開燈時漫光會照亮整張紙.	immersed only a regular piece of paper around its edges , and this immersion of photosylenecolored paper that illuminates the entire sheet of paper when we open the light .
就目前所知 , 這種材料已經被應用到室內設計和多點觸控系統兩個領域中了 。	as far as we know , this material has been applied to interior design and multiple touch systems .
而熱變色顏料在特定的溫度下會改變顏色 。	and thermal pigments change colors under certain temperatures .
我先把這張東西放到一個電熱板上溫度設定比外界溫度稍高一點然後你可以看到發生了什麼.	i'm going to put this thing on a board and set up a temperature slightly higher temperature than outside , and you can see what's going on .
除了其它用途 , 這種材料主要用作嬰兒奶瓶的製造 。 它能告訴你什麼時候瓶裡的東西涼到可飲用的溫度 。	except for other uses , this material makes a baby bottle , and it tells you when things are cool to drinking .
這些就是我們通常所說的 " 智慧材料 " 的幾個例子 。	these are just a few examples of what we often call smart materials .
幾年內 , 它們將被應用到很多我們日常使用的物件和科技產品上 。	within a few years , they're going to be applied to so many things and technological products that we use every day .
我們也許還不會有科幻小說向我們保證的飛行汽車 , 但是我們能擁有隨溫度變色的牆 , 可以捲起來的鍵盤 , 和一<unk>開關就變不透明的窗戶 。	we may not have science fiction yet to promise our flying cars , but we can have walls with temperature changes that can roll up the keyboard and a possibility that's shrink to the world that's very clear .
我是科班出身的社會科學家 , 為什麼今天我在這裡講智慧材料 ?	i'm a social scientist in the class , why am i talking about smart materials today ?
首先 , 我是個製造者 。	first , i'm a maker .
我對於東西如何運轉和怎樣製作有好奇心 , 我也相信我們應該對我們這個世界的組成材料有更深的瞭解 , 並且現在 , 我們對於這些構成我們未來的高科技材料瞭解不多 。	i'm curious about how things work and how they make curiosity , and i'm also convinced that we should have a deeper understanding of the materials of our world , and right now , we don't know much about these hightech materials that make up our future .
要獲得少量的智慧材料是很難的 。	it's hard to get a small amount of smart material .
有關如何使用這些材料的資訊也很少 , 它們是如何製作的資訊就更加少得可憐 。	information about how to use these materials very few , and how they make less information .
目前 , 它們絕大多數都存在於貿易機密和專利中 , 只有大學和大公司才能得到 。	currently , most of them exist in trade secrets and patents , only universities and large companies .
所以三年多以前 , 我和kirstyboyle發起了一個叫做openmaterials的專案 。	so three years ago , i and kirstyboy boyle launched a project called the openmaterialials .
在那個網站上 , 我們和想要加入我們的任何人 , 分享實驗 , 釋出資訊 , 鼓勵其他人為此作出力所能及的貢獻 , 並且收集像研究論文和像我們一樣的製造者所製作的教程一類的資源 。	on that website , we and we join anyone who wants to join us , sharing experiments , encouraging others to contribute to the contributions that we can do for this , and collect programs like the work papers and the makers of resources like ours .
我們希望把這一網站做成一個大規模的、集體生成的資料庫 , 蒐集用智慧材料diy的資訊 。	we wanted to make this site as a largescale , collective database of databases collecting smart material diy's information .
但是我們為什麼要關心智慧材料是如何工作和它們是用什麼來製造的呢 ?	but why do we care about how intelligent materials work and what are they using ?
首先 , 因為我們無法影響我們不理解的東西 , 我們不理解和不會用的東西還會反過來影響我們 。	first , because we can't influence what we don't understand , we don't understand and use things that don't work in the opposite way .
我們使用的東西 , 我們穿的衣服 , 我們住的房子 , 都對我們的行為、健康和生活質量上產生深遠的影響 。	what we're using , the clothes we're wearing , the houses we live in , have a profound impact on our behavior , our health and our life mass .
所以如果我們將要生活在一個由智慧材料構成的世界中 , 我們就應該知道並瞭解它們 。	so if we're going to live in a world made of smart materials , we should know and understand them .
第二 , 同樣重要地 , 創新總是來源於修補匠 。	secondly , just as importantly , innovation comes from substitutes .
很多時候 , 是業餘愛好者而非專家 , 發明和改進了諸如山地車、半導體、個人電腦、甚至飛機 。	in many cases , amateurs rather than experts , invention and improvements like mountain cars , semiconductors , personal computers , even airplanes .
材料科學的最大挑戰是它的複雜性 , 以及對昂貴的儀器的需求 。	the biggest challenge of material science is its complexity and the need for expensive instruments .
但事實並非總如此 。	but that's not always the case .
伊利諾伊大學的兩名科學家在他們發表一篇關於用更簡便的方法制作導電墨水的論文時就明白了這個道理 。	two scientists at the university of illinois published a paper about manufacturing conductive inks that understood .

他用了一個烤箱 , 而且他甚至在另一個科學家/製造者的教程的基礎上自制了旋渦混合器 。	he uses a oven , and he even autonomously autonomously at the basis of another scientist's original engine .
後來 , jordan在網上發表了他的實驗結果 , 包括所有他試過的沒成功的東西 , 這樣其他人可以學習然後複製這一實驗 。	and then jordan published his experiment online , including all the things he tried , so that others could learn and replicate this experiment .
所以jordan主要創新方式是拿一個在設施齊全的大學實驗室裡創造的實驗 , 然後在芝加哥的一個車庫裡用便宜材料和自制的工具來重複實驗 。	so the main innovation of jordan is to take an experiment that's created in a university laboratory in a garage in chicago with inexpensive materials and autonomous tools .
在他發表的實驗結果基礎上 , 其他人可以接著做下去並且設計甚至更簡單的步驟和改進實驗 。	on the basis of his experiments , others could go on and design even simpler steps and improve experiments .
我想分享的另外一個例子她專案的目標是在突出材料富有表現力的特質的同時專注於製造者的創造力和製造技巧 。	another example i'd like to share with you is that the goal of her program is to emerge the traits of materials that are performing expressively focused on creativity and manufacturing skills
電子工具在教我們東西如何運轉這方面非常有力 , 但是它們設計中傳承下來的約束影響我們學習的方式 。	electronic tools teach us very powerful in how to operate , but the constraints that they're designing have influenced the way we learn .
所以hannah的方法 , 在另一方面 , 就是創制一系列的技術 , 來創造非常規的東西 , 透過教給我們材料本身的知識 , 把我們從事先設計好的約束中解放出來 。	so hannah's approach , on the other hand , is to create a series of technologies to create something very regular , and by teaching our material materials to liberate us from our preconstraints .
在hannah眾多令人欽佩的試驗中 , 這個是我的最愛之一 。	this is one of my favorites in hannah's admirable experiment .
[ " 會說話的紙 " ]我們在這裡看到的只不過是一張紙上面的銅帶連線著一個mp3播放器和一塊磁鐵 。	[ " talking to paper " ] what we're seeing here is just a piece of paper on a piece of paper with a mp3 player and a piece of magnets .
在麻省理工學院教授marcelocoelho研究的基礎上 , hannah使用各種材料創造了一系列紙質揚聲器 。 從普通的銅帶到導電的織物和墨水 ,	on the basis of the mit professor marcelocoelho research , hannah uses a series of materials to create a series of paper speakers , from the normal copper to the fabric and ink .
就像jordan和其他很多製造者一樣 , hannah發表了她的配方並且允許任何人來重複這些實驗 。	like jordan and many other makers , hannah published her recipe and allowed anyone to repeat these experiments .
但是紙上電子是材料科學中最有前景的分支之一 , 因為它讓我們能創造出便宜又靈活的電子產品 。	but paper electrons are one of the most promising branches of material science , because it allows us to create cheap and flexible electronics .
所以hannah的手工作品 , 和她分享了她的發現這個事實 , 打開了一扇門 , 通向兼具美學和創新的一系列新的可能 。	so hannah's handwork , shared her findings with her , opened a door to a new series of aesthetic and innovative possibilities .
製造者的有趣之處在於我們創造是出於熱情和好奇 , 並且我們不害怕失敗 。	what's interesting about makers is that we create passion and curiosity and we're not afraid of failure .
我們通常從非傳統的角度處理問題 , 並且 , 在這個過程中 , 最終發現其他方案或者更好的方法 。	we often deal with problems from nontraditional angles , and in this process , we end up finding other solutions or better approaches .
所以當更多的人願意用新材料做試驗的時候 , 更多的研究者就會願意分享他們的研究成果 ; 有更多的製造商分享他們的知識 , 我們就會有更好的機會來創造造福我們所有人的科技 。	so when more people are willing to experiment with new materials , more researchers are willing to share their research ; more manufacturers are sharing their knowledge , we'll have better opportunities to create technologies for all of us .
我的感覺有一點像tednelson在70年代初期的感覺一樣 , 他寫道 , " 你們現在必需懂電腦 。 "	i felt a little bit like the feeling of tednelson in the early '70s , and he wrote , " you need to understand computers now . "
那個時候 , 電腦是這些只有科學家關心的大型機 , 沒有人會夢想到放一臺在家裡 。	at that point , computers were these big machines that were concerned with scientists , and nobody would dream of putting a place in the house .
所以我今天站在這裡說 " 你們現在必需懂智慧材料 " 有一點奇怪 。	so i'm standing here today and saying , " you need to understand smart materials , " which is a little bit strange .
請記住對於新興科技擁有先發制人的知識是確保我們在對未來的創造中有發言權的最好方式 。	remember that knowledge of emerging technologies have the best way to ensure that we have a voice in the future .
當我們開車是 , 我們就坐進了一個玻璃氣泡中 , 鎖上門 , 踩下油門 , 依靠眼睛為我們自己導航 。 即使我們僅僅只能看見車前車後的幾輛車 。 但是假如汽車能互換關於位置、速度的資料 , 並運用預測模型來為每一位司機測算最安全的線路呢 ? 詹妮佛海麗構想了一個零車禍的世界 。	when we drive , we're sitting in a glass bubble , locking up the door , stepping on the oil door , navigating ourselves , even if we just see a couple of cars behind the front car , but if cars can switch each other on the speed of position , and predict the safest route for every driver ?
詹妮弗海麗:汽車若能交流車禍或可避免	jennifer hay: automobiles can communicate crashes or avoid .
讓我們來面對一樁事實吧開車是一件危險的事	let's face the fact that driving is a dangerous thing .
它是我們不願意去想的事物之一但事實上那些神像和平安符世界各地都有人把它們擺在儀表盤的上方這就無意中透露出一個我們都心知肚明的事實	it's one of the things that we don't want to think about , but in fact , those gods like peace and security all over the world have people putting them on the top of the scale , and it's unintended to reveal a reality that we all know .
車禍是死亡的主因尤其在美國16到19歲的美國人群中死亡的主因並且百分之七十五的車禍都與毒品和酒精無關	car accidents are the leading cause of death , especially in the united states 16 to 19 years old , and 75 percent of car accidents have nothing to do with drugs and alcohol .
沒人能給出確切答案但我記得我第一次出車禍	nobody can give the exact answer , but i remember getting out of a car accident for the first time .
我當時還是個開車的新手 , 當時正在外面高速路上開著車 。 我突然看見我前面汽車的剎車燈亮了	i was driving as a new hand , and i was driving on the highway , and all of a sudden , i saw the brake lights in front of me .
我當時想好吧他減速了那我也減速好了	and i thought , well , he's speeding up , and i'll slow down .
我踩了剎車	i stepped on the brake .
但是我前面那個人並不是在減速	but the person in front of me is not about slowing down .
他停車了突然停車在高速路上突然停車	he parked and suddenly parked on the highway , and all of a sudden ,
速度從65邁瞬降到0	it goes from 65 miles to zero .
我猛踩剎車	i stood on a brake .
我當時感覺到我的車的防抱死系統啟動了但車還在行駛並沒停下來的意思我也知道我的車停不了了安全氣囊也鼓了起來車報廢了但幸運的是沒有人受傷	i felt like my car was initiated , but the car was still initiating , and i knew that my car parked , and the airbags pushed up , but fortunately nobody was injured .
但我根本不知道我前面那輛車要停而且我想我們可以比那做得更好	but i didn't even know i was parking in front of that car , and i think we could do better than that .
我想我們透過實現 " 讓汽車之間對話 " 來改變我們的駕駛體驗	i think we're going to change the experience of the driver by making the car dialogue .
我希望你們能思考片刻思考一下現在的駕駛體驗是怎麼樣的	i hope you'll be able to think about how the driver's experience is right now .
坐進車裡關上車門你就已經置身在一個玻璃氣泡中	sitting in the car and closing the door , you're already in a glass bubble .
你不能直接感受到你周圍的世界	you can't just feel the world around you .
因為你坐在車這樣一個不小的空間裡	because you're sitting in a very tiny space like this .
你的任務就是導航你只能看見道路的一部分並且以超人類的速度行駛在其他的 " 金屬巨人 " 間	your mission is to navigate , you can only see a part of the road , and travel at superhuman speeds in other metal giants .
對吧 ? 你只能靠雙眼來導航	right ? you can navigate with your eyes .
對你別無他法眼睛並非是用來幹著活兒的但是有些事情你就必須得做 , 比方說 , 你想換個車道那你第一件要做的事是什麼	for you , it's not for you to do something that's alive , but there's something you have to do , for example , you want to change a car , and what you're going to do in the first place .
將眼睛從車道上移開對	remove the eyes from the road .

mit研究人員斯凱拉•蒂比茨從事自我裝配的研究一個取代建造東西的主意 , 我們能創建制作自己的材料 , 很像dna鏈打包的方式 。 目前還是一個巨大概念的早期階段 ; 蒂比茨向我們展示了三個還在實驗中的專案 , 我們可以一窺一個自我裝配的未來可能的樣子 。	researchers at mit stella tibitz , who works on selfassembly , is an idea to replace things , and we can create materials that build our materials , very much like dna chains , and currently it's an early stage of concept ; tibitz shows us three projects in the experiment , and we can look at a possible future of selfassembly possible .
斯凱拉•蒂比茨:我們能製作可以製作自己的東西麼 ?	scerra tips: can we make what we can make ?
今天我想向各位展示未來我們製作東西的方式 。	today i'd like to show you the way we make things in the future .
我相信很快我們的建築和機器將能自我組裝 , 自我複製和自我修復 。	i believe that soon our buildings and machines can selfassemble , selfrepair and selfrepair .
因此我要向各位展示我所認為的製造業的當前狀況 , 接著再將其與一些自然系統比較 。	so i'm going to show you what i think is the current state of manufacturing , and then compare it to some natural systems .
那麼在當前的製造業中 , 我們有摩天大樓兩年半的時間 , 50萬至上百萬個部分 , 非常複雜 , 使用了在鋼鐵 , 混凝土和玻璃方面的新技術 。	so in the current manufacturing , we have skyscrapers for two and a half years , five million to millions , very complicated , using new techniques in steel , concrete and glass .
我們有令人激動的機器 , 可以帶我們進入太空五年時間 , 兩百五十萬個部分 。	we have exciting machines that can take us into space for five years , 2 . 5 million parts .
但另一方面 , 如果看看自然系統 , 我們有擁有兩百萬種類型的蛋白質 , 能在一萬納秒內摺疊起來 , 我們能在大約一小時內對帶有三十億鹼基對的dna進行復制 。	but on the other hand , if you look at the natural system , we have two million types of proteins that can fold up in 10 , 000 nanoseconds , we can recover in about an hour with three billion base pairs of dna .
這就是我們自然系統的複雜性 , 但它們非常高效 , 比我們建造的任何東西都要高效 , 比我們能建造的任何東西都要複雜 。	this is the complexity of our natural system , but they're very efficient , much more efficient than anything we build , much more complicated than anything we can build .
它們在能源方面更加高效 。	they're more efficient in terms of energy .
它們很少犯錯 。	they rarely make mistakes .
他們能自我修復保持長壽 。	they can repair their longevity .
關於自然系統有件超級有意思的事情 。	there's a really interesting thing about the natural system .
如果我們能將其轉換為我們的建築環境 , 那麼我們構建事物的方式就會有很大的潛力 。	if we can convert it into our construction environment , then the way we build things will be enormous potential .
我認為關鍵是自我組裝 。	i think the key is selfassembly .
如果我們想要在自身的身體環境中利用自我組裝 , 我認為有四個關鍵因素 。	if we want to use selfassembly in our own environment , i think there are four key factors .
第一個是 , 我們需要解碼我們所要建造的東西的所有的複雜度也就是我們的建築和機器 。	the first is that we need to decode all the complexity of what we're going to build is our architecture and machines .
我們需要把它們解碼成簡單的序列基本上就是我們的建築運作的dna 。	we need to decode them into simple sequences that are basically the dna of our buildings working .
接著我們需要可程式設計的部分這部分能接受這一序列並用於摺疊或是重塑 。	and then we need parts of programmable design that accept that sequence and use folding or reshaping .
我們需要一些能量來進行啟用 , 使我們的這些部分能夠依照程式摺疊起來 。	we need some energy to activate , so that our parts can fold up based on programming .
我們需要一些型別的糾錯冗餘以保證我們成功建造的就是我們想要的 。	we need some other entanglement redundancy to guarantee that we're successfully building is what we want .
因此 , 我要向各位展示一些我和我的同事正在進行的要實現這種自我組裝的未來的專案 。	so i'm going to show you some of the projects that my colleagues and i are working on in the future of selfassembly projects .
頭兩個專案是macrobot和decibot 。	the first two projects are macrobot and decibot .
這些專案都是大規模可重構機器人8英尺 , 12英尺長的蛋白質 。	these projects are largescale robots , eight feet , 12 feet long .
它們嵌入機電裝置 , 感測器 。	they embedded organic devices , sensors .

每個要用於計算的門上都有一個四面體 , 有兩個輸入四面體 。	each door to computing has a quadriple , two inputs .

接著它會給出三維空間的輸出 。	and then it gives a threedimensional output .
這意味著使用者以他們想要的方式堆砌磚塊 。	that means user building bricks in the way they want .
它依據之前所做的和你的指令進行計算 。	it calculates based on what you've done and what you commands before .
現在它開始在三維空間內移動上或者下 。	now it starts moving in threedimensional spaces , or underneath .
看左面 , [1 , 1]的輸入等於0輸出 , 表示向下 。	look at the lefthand side , [1 , one] input equals output equivalent to zero output , which means down .
在右邊 , [0 , 0]的輸入是1輸出 , 表示向上 。	on the right , [0 , 0] input is one output , and that's upward .
因此這真正的的意味是我們的結構中現在包含了我們想要構建的藍圖 。	so what this really means is that our structure now includes the blueprints that we want to build .
因此關於想要構建的事物的資訊已經全部嵌入其中 。	so the information about what you want to build is all embedded .
這意味著我們有了某種形式的自我複製 。	that means we have some form of selfreplication .
對這種情況 , 我稱之為自我導向複製 , 因為你的結構中包含了精確的藍圖 。	in this case , i call this selfdirection copying , because your structure contains a precise blueprint of your structure .
如果遇到錯誤 , 你可以替換一個部分 。	if you have a mistake , you can replace a part .

如果我們想成為例外的話 , 邏輯上來看我們唯一的希望是利用將我們這個種群和文明與其他物種區別開的這個特徵 , 與其他一切都區別開的這個特徵 。 也就是 , 我們與物理定律得特殊關係 。 我們創造新的解釋和知識的能力--成為存在的中心 。	if we want to be an exception , logically to look at our only hope is to distinguish the characteristics of our species and our civilization and other species that distinguish the characteristics of everything else , and that is , we have a special relationship to the laws of physics , and we create new explanations and knowledge central to existence .

這個論戰就是全球暖化 。	this argument is global warming .
我是一個物理學家 , 但我並不是此領域的物理學家 。 就全球暖化來說 , 我只是個門外漢 。 對一個門外漢來說理智的做法是嚴肅對待權威的科學理論 。 而根據這一理論 , 已經太晚了 , 災難在所難免 。	i'm a physicist , but i'm not a physicist in the field , and in terms of global warming , i'm just an outsider , and it's a scientific theory of seriously treated authority , and according to this theory , it's too late for disaster .
因為 , 如果我們目前最好的選擇是阻止二氧化碳排放的話 , 例如透過東京議定書之類的 , 限制經濟活動 , 以及花費千億美元等巨大的代價 , 那麼不管如何衡量 , 這就已經是一個災難了 。	because if the best option is to stop carbon dioxide emissions , for example , through tokyo and so on , restricting economic activity and spending hundreds of billions of dollars , it's already a disaster .
倡議的行動甚至都不是為解決問題 , 而只是稍微推遲災難的到來 。 因此災難在所難免 , 一切都已晚 , 或在所有人意識到這個危險之前就已經太晚了 。	advocates aren't even solving the problem , it's just a slightly pushing a little bit , so the catastrophic disaster is inevitably late , or it's already too late for everyone to recognize this danger .
上世紀70年代的時候也許就已經太晚了 , 那時候最先進的科學理論告訴我們工業排放將促成一個新的冰河世紀 , 數十億的人類將從此滅亡 。	it may have been too late in the '70s , and the most advanced scientific theory tells us that industrial emissions are going to push a new glacier century , and billions of people will die .
這一教訓對我來說清晰可見 , 我不明白為什麼它沒有傳達至公眾辯論 。	the lesson was clear to me , and i don't understand why it didn't communicate public debate .
事實是我們不可能永遠知道 。 當我們知道有一個災難將要降臨 , 應對這個災難的成本要比災難本身小 , 那麼就真的沒有什麼好爭論的 。	the fact is that we're never going to know that when we know that there's a disaster that's going to respond to the cost of this disaster , there's no good argument .

因此我們需要準備好去解決問題 , 而不僅僅是避免問題 。	so we need to be ready to solve the problem , not just avoiding the problem .
一盎司的預防等於一盎司的解決 , 這是事實 , 但是這只是在我們知道預防什麼的情況下 。	a ounce of prevention is equivalent to an ounce of solutions , and that's true , but it's just that we know what to prevent .

大多數人沒有意識到這些肉眼看不到的生物微生物構成了地球約一半的生物量而所有的動物加起來也才佔地球生物量的千分之一	most of us don't realize that these microbes can't see them make up about half the biomass of the earth , and all the animals combined together to account for one thousandth of the biomass of the planet .

採集海水 , 過濾用不同的過濾器採集不同大小的生物然後把它們的dna帶回羅克韋爾的實驗室在那裡我們可以每24小時測完一億字元的遺傳編碼	take seawater , filter it with different filters , collect different sizes , and then bring their dna back to rockwell's laboratory , where we can measure 100 million letters of genetic coding every 24 hours .
透過這些我們已經有了一些驚人的發現	and through that , we have some amazing discoveries .

僅僅一個採集點 , 從一桶水中我們就能發現1300萬個新基因相當於5萬個新種	in a single gathering point , we can see that 1 . 3 million new genes are equivalent to 50 , 000 new species .
藉助來自斯隆基金會的資助我們已經將研究擴充套件到空氣中	by funding the sloan foundation , we've expanded the research into the air .
我們正在測算 , 在我們每天呼吸的空氣中漂浮著多少病毒和細菌特別是在飛機和禮堂等封閉環境中	we're calculating how much viruses and bacteria floating in the air that we breathe every day , especially in the airplanes and in the auditorium .
我們透過一些簡單的儀器進行過濾在紐約市某棟建築的頂上僅用一天我們就過濾出數十億計的微生物	we've been filtering hundreds of millions of microbes through some simple instruments in a building in new york city , using only one day , we filter billions of microbes .
目前我們正在對它們進行測序	we're now sequencing them .
單純從資料蒐集方面僅僅在加拉帕戈斯群島我們就發現幾乎每200英里我們都能從採集的樣品中看到巨大的多樣性	just in the data collection , just in the galapagos islands , we found that almost every 200 miles , we can see a huge diversity of diversity from the samples .
不同的溫度梯度或許可以部分解釋這種多樣性	different temperatures may be explained to you in some sense of diversity .
這是一張基於溫度的衛星圖片紅色表示溫暖區域藍色表示冷的區域我們發現 , 在溫暖海水中獲得樣品與冷海水中的樣品在物種的豐富程度上具有極大的差異	this is a satellite image based on the temperature , and the red shows the warm areas , and the blue , we find that samples and samples in the warm water are extremely different from the abundance of the species .
另一個讓我們感到驚奇的事情是這些光受體能探測到不同波長的光而我們能透過它們的氨基酸序列來推測這一過程	the other thing that surprised us is that these light receptors can detect light from different wavelengths , and we can infer that process through their amino acid sequence .
不同區域之間 , 它們也差別巨大	different areas , they're also enormously different .

而當週圍存在大量葉綠素的時候它們則 " 看 " 到許多綠光	and when there's lots of chlorophyll , they look like lots of green light .
在向較極端的紅外和紫外波段移動時光受體的差別可能更大	the difference between moving towards extreme infrared and ultraviolet waves can be even bigger .
為了對我們採集的所有基因進行評估我們彙總了所有資料包括到目前為止考察所得的所有資料代表了地球上超過一半的基因資料總共約2900萬個基因	to estimate all the genes that we've been gathering , we've summarized all the data , including all the data from the expedition , which means that more than half the genetic data on the planet .
我們把這些基因放入基因家族中試圖回答:我們是發現了已知基因家族中的新成員還是發現了新的基因家族 ?	we put these genes into the genomic family and tried to answer: are we discovering new genetic family members of the known genetic family or new genetic family ?
結果表明我們找到了大約5萬個主要的基因家族但我們從環境中獲得的每個新樣品都只是對這些新基因家族的線性補充	it turns out that we've found about 50 , 000 major genes , but every new sample we've gained from the environment is just a linear complement for these new genes .
因此我們正處在發現地球生命及其組成部分和基因基礎的最初階段	so we're in the first stage of discovering life on earth and its ingredients and genetic basis .
我們來看下所謂的進化樹我們人類就在右上角 , 和動物們在一起	let's look at what's called evolutionary trees , and we humans are in the upper righthand corner with animals .
在動物界約2900萬個基因中我們的基因組才僅僅擁有24000個基因	in the animal kingdom , about 29 million genes , our genome has only 2 , 400 genes .
如果把所有的動物算在一起我們與之分享著不到30000可能在1.2萬或再多數千的不同的基因家族	if we compute all the animals together , we share less than 300 , 000 genetic families with less than 120 , 000 different genetic families .
現在我不僅僅將這些基因視為進化的設計元件	now , i don't just think of these genes as evolutionary design components .
而且我們要從 " 基因中心觀點 " 或許要追溯到理查德•道金斯的理論而非 " 基因組中心觀點 " 來思考它們對這些基因元件的構造方式是不同的	and we're going to go back to the theory of genecentrics , perhaps , to the theory of richard dawkins , rather than the genome center to think about how they're made of these genetic components .
合成dna , 即人工合成dna的能力在過去的十年或二十年裡與dna測序的能力在某種程度上是同步發展的而且都變得越來越快速和廉價	synthetic dna , the ability to synthesize dna in artificial synthesis synthetic dna in the last decade or two decades and sequencing dna sequencing in some way is increasingly rapid and
有關合成基因組的想法是在1995年我們對第二個基因組即生殖道支原體測序的時候想到的	the idea of synthetic genome was that in 1995 , we thought about the second genome sequencing the second genome , the colonial support prototype .
我們還製作了相當不錯的t恤寫著 , " 我愛惜我的生殖器 "	and we made a pretty good tshirt , and it said , " i love my genitals . "
這其實只不過是個微小的生物	it's just a tiny creature .
卻擁有近500個基因	they have nearly 500 genes .
嗜血桿菌擁有1800個基因	blood rods have 1 , 800 genes .
我們提出疑問如果某物種需要800個基因 , 另一種需要500個是否能用一套更小的基因組成一個微小的可運作生命系統	we said , " if a species needs 800 genes , the other one requires 500 genes , whether a lifestyle is made up of a smaller set of genomes . "
於是我們開始做轉座子的突變發生	so we started to make a mutation in the consequence of the seat .
轉座子是隨機插入遺傳編碼之中的短的dna片段	the contact is randomly inserts the short piece of dna from the genetic code .
如果轉座子插入到基因中間 , 就會擾亂基因的功能	if you insert it in the middle of the gene , it disrupts the function of the genes .
因此我們找出所有能夠接受轉座子插入的基因併為這些 " 非必需基因 " 製作了 " 地圖 "	so we figured out all the genes that could be inserted into these genes , not necessary genes , made maps .
但結果我們發現環境對此的影響非常關鍵我們只能根據環境中確實存在的條件來定義必需和非必需基因	but it turns out that the environment is very critical to this , and we can only define genes according to the conditions that exist in the environment .
我們還試圖做一個更直觀的研究對13個有親緣關係的生物我們試圖比較它們的基因組 , 看它們是否有相同之處	we also tried to do a more straightforward study for 13 organisms with relational relations , and we tried to compare their genomes to see if they shared the same thing .
於是我們得到了這些重疊的圓圈 , 我們發現只有173個基因在這所有13種生物中是相同的	so we got these overlapping circles , and we found that there are only 173 genes in all 13 organisms .
如果忽略掉一個細胞內寄生物的話這個基因庫還能擴充套件一點當我們審視核心的一組約310個基因時基因庫擴大更多	if we ignore the organisms inside a cell , this genetic bank can also expand a little bit when we look at the core of a team of about 310 genes .
因此我們認為可以從最少500個基因擴充套件或縮小取決你怎麼看這個問題到約300到400個基因	so we think we can expand from the minimum 500 genes , or shrink depending on how you see this problem , about 300 to 400 genes .
證明這些理論的唯一方法是以這些基因人工構建一個染色體而且我們必須用基於表達框的方式來達到這一目的	the only way to prove these theories is to construct a chromosome in these genes , and we have to use that based on the boxes .
我們發現大片段精確合成dna是非常非常困難的	it turns out that big pieces of synthetic dna are very , very difficult .
我的同事漢姆•史密斯和克萊德•哈欽森發明了一個讓人振奮的新方法能讓我們在短短兩週時間內合成一個擁有5000個鹼基對的病毒而且在基因序列和生物學特性上都百分百精確	my colleague , hanm smith and keled harginson , invented an exciting new way of synthesizing a virus with 50 , 000 base pairs of base pairs in just two weeks , and specifically in genomic sequences and biology .
那是個相當讓人興奮的實驗:我們僅僅把合成的dna片段注進細菌中 , 突然之間dna就開始引導病毒顆粒的合成而病毒反過來殺死了細菌	it was a very exciting experiment: we just injected the synthetic piece of dna into the bacteria , and all of a sudden dna started to guide the synthetic particles of the virus , and the viruses killed the bacteria .
這並非第一個合成的病毒一年前已有某種脊髓灰質炎病毒被製造了出來但這卻是唯一達到百分之一活性的病毒耗時三年才合成成功	this is not the first synthetic virus that had been produced a spinal cord virus a year ago , but it was the only synthesis of a third of active viruses in three years .

基本上 , 任何現在已經被測序的病毒其基因組都可以被合成	basically , any viral genome that's sequenced now can be synthesized .
人們立馬被埃博拉病毒或天花病毒之類等嚇壞了但從這些生物體中提取的dna並不具有感染力	people immediately frightened by ebola virus or smallpox , but the dna extracted from these organisms is not infectious .
因此即使有人制成了天花病毒基因組其dna本身並不會引發感染	so even if someone made a smallpox genome , the dna itself doesn't cause infections .
安全部門真正需要擔心的是 " 設計者病毒 "	the security sector really needs to worry about the design virus .
只有兩個國家 , 美國和前蘇聯曾經花大力氣致力於生物武器的研製	only two countries , the united states and the former soviet union , have spent a lot of effort working on biological weapons .
如果這些研究真的已經終止那麼在未來人為製造出設計者病毒的機率微乎其微	if those studies have actually stopped , then the probability of people to make design viruses in the future is very tiny .
我想兩年內製造出單細胞生物是可能的	i think it's possible to make singlecell organisms in two years .
而真核細胞我們自己擁有的這種細胞也可能在十年內製造出來	and the nuclear cells that we have in our own own cells can also be produced in 10 years .
我們可以區分開進入這個人工基因組的不同表達框和不同基因使得我們能構建數十種不同的結構	we can separate into this artificial genome , expressing frames and different genes , so we can build dozens of different structures .
關鍵是 , 如何把所有其他的放進來 ?	and the key is , how do you put all the other things in ?

時間洞察力是研究個人包括我們在內 , 如何以時間區域或時間類別為單位劃分自身的經歷體驗 。	time insight is about studying individuals , including how we're categorizing our experiences in time zones or time categories .

對一些人來說 , 這個決定只是基於現狀另一些人是基於他們的直覺 。	for some people , this decision was just based on the status quo , and other people were based on their intuition .
對於那些基於現狀而做決定的人我們稱呼他們為: " 面向現在 " 因為他們專注於現正發生的事情	for the people who make the decisions based on the status quo , we call them " facetoface , " because they focus on what's happening right now .

那你就具有某種程度上的片面的時間洞察力	so you have some kind of sight insight .
實際上是有六種時間洞察力 , 其中兩個屬於 " 面向現在 "	in fact , there are six times of insight , two of them belong to the present .

他們反映說那些從未加入任何運動的以色列人看了紀錄片之後瞭解了非暴力抵抗的力量並開始加入他們行動	they reflected that the israelis who never joined any movement had seen a documentary , understood the power of nonviolent resistance and started joining them .
瓦拉傑和索裡德拉爾特運動的例子告訴我們即使是小成本的獨立電影也能夠幫助非暴力抵抗轉變為一種功能性行為	the example of the valadger and sordalt movement tells us that even a small , independent film can help nonviolent resistance to a functional behavior .
想象一下主流媒體若是開始報道每週在貝拉因尼亞林瓦拉傑等村莊以及耶路撒冷境內的香克哈拉和西路萬巴勒斯坦居住區裡發生的非暴力示威活動這將產生多麼巨大的力量更多的人會關注非暴力運動領導者重視他們讓他們的工作更有成效	if you think about mainstream media , if it's starting to report on the villages of bella lincia , and so forth in jerusalem , the nonviolent demonstrations that are happening in the western palestinian region , it's going to be a lot more people who care about nonviolent movement leaders respecting their work more effectively .

但我以親身經歷為證如果我們關注這些運動就會得到發展	but i promise myself , if we look at these movements , we'll be developed .
它們一旦發展其影響力就會遍及巴以衝突	and once they develop it , they go through the palestinian conflict .
這種影響能夠最終將衝突化解	this effect ultimately conflicts conflict .
這些領導者證明了非暴力運動在佈德魯斯這樣的地方是可行的	these leaders proved that nonviolent movements work in places like treus .
我們一起來關注他們讓他們證明這在任何地方都是可行的	and we focused on them , and we showed them that it works everywhere .
西蒙•斯涅克用一個簡單但是震撼的模型來闡釋激勵人心的領袖力 , 這個模型的核心是一個 " 黃金 " 圓圈 , 意思是領袖素質的根本來源是回答 " 為什麼 ? " 。 他列舉了蘋果公司、馬丁•路德•金還有萊特兄弟成功的例子 , 同時以蒂沃數碼錄影機為失敗的典型 。 雖然蒂沃最近打贏一場官司 , 使得其股價上漲了3倍 , 但是它仍在掙扎中 。	simone steenneck used a simple , but shocked model to illustrate the leadership of the incentive , which is a golden circle , which means the fundamental source of leadership is , " why ? " he listed an apple , martin luther king and the wright brothers , typically winning a typical typical of a digital recorder , and although it's recently doubled to a price , but it's still 3 .
bullseye , business , entrepreneur , leadership , sales , selling , success	bullsey , and it's going to be , and it's going to be noise , sales , selling , success .
西蒙•斯涅克:偉大的領袖如何激勵行動	simone senak: how great leaders inspire action .
當事情的發展出乎意料之外的時候 , 你怎麼解釋 ?	how do you explain when things are developing unexpectedly ?
換句話說 , 當別人似乎出乎意料地取得成功的時候 , 你怎麼解釋 ?	in other words , what do you explain when people seem to be surprisingly achieved success ?
比如說 , 為什麼蘋果公司創新能力這麼強 ?	for example , why are apple companies so innovatively innovative ?
這麼多年來 , 年復一年 , 他們比所有競爭對手都更加具有創新性 。	over the years , over the years , they've been more innovative than all competition opponents .
而其實他們只是一家電腦公司 。	and they're actually just a computer company .
他們跟其他公司沒有任何分別 ,	they don't have any differences with other companies .
有同樣的途徑 , 接觸到同樣的人才 , 同樣的代理商 , 顧問 , 和媒體 。	there's the same approach to the same people , the same agenda , consultants and media .
那為什麼他們就似乎有那麼一點不同尋常呢 ?	so why do they seem to be so different ?
同樣的 , 為什麼是由馬丁•路德•金來領導民權運動 ?	again , why is that martin luther king to lead the civil rights movement ?
那個時候在美國 , 民權運動之前 , 不僅僅只有他一個人飽受歧視 。 他也決不是那個時代唯一的偉大演說家 。	at that time , before the united states , the civil rights movement was not just one person being discriminated , but he was also determined that he wasn't the only greatest speaker of that time .
又為什麼懷特兄弟能夠造出動力控制的載人飛機 , 跟他們相比 , 當時的其他團隊似乎更有能力 , 更有資金 ,	and why is it that the white brothers are able to create a dynamic controlled airplane compared to the other teams that seemed to be more capable and more funded ?
他們卻沒能製造出載人飛機 , 懷特兄弟打敗了他們 。	they didn't make a carrier plane , and the white brothers beat them .
一定還有一些什麼別的因素在起作用 。	there's something else that's going to work .
大概三年半之前 , 我有了個新發現 ,	about three and a half years ago , i had a new discovery .
這個發現完全改變了我對這個世界如何運作的看法 。 甚至從根本上改變了我的工作生活方式 。	this discovery completely changed my perception of how the world works , and even fundamentally changed my way of working .
那就是我發現了一種模式 ,	and that's what i found .
我發現世界上所有偉大的令人振奮的領袖和組織 , 無論是蘋果公司、馬丁•路德•金還是懷特兄弟 , 他們思考、行動、交流溝通的方式都完全一樣 ,	i found that all of the great leaders and organizations in the world , whether it's apple , martin luther king or the white brothers , they think , action and communication are exactly the same way .
但是跟所有其他人的方式完全相反 。	but the opposite of all the other people .
我所做的僅僅是把它整理出來 。 這可能是世上最簡單的概念 。	all i'm doing is just fixing it . it's probably the easiest concept in the world .
我稱它為黃金圓環 。	i call it the golden circle .
為什麼 ? 怎麼做 ? 是什麼 ?	why ? how ? what ? what ?
這小小的模型就解釋了為什麼一些組織和領導者能夠在別人不能的地方激發出靈感和潛力 。	this little model explains why some organizations and leaders can inspire and potential in places where others can't .
我來儘快地解釋一下這些術語 。	i'm going to explain these terms as quickly as possible .
地球上的每個人 , 每個組織都明白自己做的是什麼 , 百分之百 。	everyone on the planet knows what they do , 100 percent .
其中一些知道該怎麼做 , 你可以稱之為是你的差異價值 , 或是你的獨特工藝 , 或是你的獨特賣點也好 , 怎麼說都行 。	some of them know what to do , you can call it your difference , or your unique craft , or your unique craft point , or your unique selling point .
但是非常 , 非常少的人和組織明白為什麼做 。	but very , very few people and organizations understand why .
這裡的 " 為什麼 " 和 " 為利潤 " 沒有關係 ,	there's nothing to do with profits .
利潤只是一個結果 , 永遠只能是一個結果 。	profit is just a result , and it's always a result .
我說的 " 為什麼 " 指的是:你的目的是什麼 ?	i'm talking about " why " i mean: what is your purpose ?
你這樣做的原因是什麼 ? 你懷著什麼樣的信念 ?	what is the reason why do you do this ? what do you believe ?
你的機構為什麼而存在 ?	why does your organization exist ?
你每天早上是為什麼而起床 ?	why did you wake up every morning ?
為什麼別人要在乎你 ?	why do people care about you ?
結果是 , 我們思考的方式 , 行動的方式 , 交流的方式都是由外向內的 。	it turns out that the way we think , the way we act , the way we interact , is by extroverts .
很顯然的 , 我們所採用的方式是從清晰開始 , 然後到模糊的東西 。	obviously , the way we do it is by starting with clarity , and then by blurry stuff .
但是激勵型領袖以及組織機構 , 無論他們的規模大小 , 所在領域 , 他們思考 , 行動和交流的方式都是從裡向外的 。	but inspiring leaders and organizations , both of them , in the field of size , they think about action and communication in the way that they're extroverted .
舉個例子吧 。	let me give you an example .
我舉蘋果公司是因為這個例子簡單易懂 , 每個人都能理解 。	i have apple company because it's easy to understand , and everyone can understand .
如果蘋果公司跟其他公司一樣 , 他們的市場營銷資訊就會是這個樣子: " 我們做最棒的電腦 ,	if apple companies like other companies , their marketing information will look like this: " we make the best computer .
設計精美 , 使用簡單 , 介面友好 。	design beautiful , using simple , interface friendly .
你想買一臺嗎 ? " 不怎麼樣吧 。	do you want to buy one ? "
這就是我們大多數人的交流方式 ,	this is how most of us interact .
也是大多數市場推廣的方式 , 大部分銷售所採用的方式 , 也是我們大部分人互相交流的方式 。	and it's the way that most of the market spreads , most of the ways that we communicate with each other .
我們說我們的職業是幹什麼的 , 我們說我們是如何的與眾不同 , 或者我們怎麼比其他人更好 , 然後我們就期待著一些別人的反應 , 比如購買 , 比如投票 , 諸如此類 。	we say what our professions are doing , we say we're different , or how we're better than others , and we're expecting some responses like buying , like voting , and so on .
這是我們新開的的律師事務所 , 我們擁有最棒的律師和最大的客戶 , 我們總是能滿足客戶的要求 。	this is our newfound lawyer affair , and we have the best lawyers and the biggest clients , and we always satisfy the demands of our clients .
這是我們的新車型 , 非常省油 , 真皮座椅 。 買一輛吧 。	this is our new car , it's very saving , it's a leather chair . buy a vehicle .
這是蘋果公司實際上的溝通方式:	this is how apple actually communicates .
" 我們做的每一件事情 , 都是為了突破和創新 。	" everything we do is to break and innovate .
我們堅信應該以不同的方式思考 。	we believe we should think differently .
我們挑戰現狀的方式是透過把我們的產品設計得十分精美 , 使用簡單 , 和介面友好 。	the way we challenge the status quo is by designing our products very beautifully , using simple , interface friendships .
我們只是在這個過程中做出了最棒的電腦 。	we just made the best computer in the process .
想買一臺嗎 ? "	would you like to buy one ? "
感覺完全不一樣 , 對吧 ? 你已經準備從我這裡買一臺了 。	it feels completely different , right ? you're ready to buy one from me .
我所做的只是將傳遞資訊的順序顛倒一下而已 。	all i'm doing is turning upside down the sequence of information .
事實已經向我們證明 , 人們買的不是你做的產品 , 人們買的是你的信念和宗旨 。	it turns out that people don't buy products you make , people buy your beliefs and your mission .
人們買的不是你做的產品 , 人們買的是你的信念 。	people don't buy products you make , people buy your beliefs .
這就解釋了為什麼這裡的每個人從蘋果公司買電腦時都覺得理所當然 。	and that explains why everyone here takes granted for granted when they buy a computer from apple company .
但是我們從蘋果公司買mp3播放器 , 手機 , 或者數碼攝像機時 , 也感覺很舒服 。	but when we bought an mp3 player from apple , a cell phone or a digital camera , it felt comfortable .
而其實 , 我剛才已經說過 , 蘋果公司只是個電腦公司 。	and actually , i've already said that apple is just a computer company .
沒有什麼能從結構上將蘋果公司同競爭對手區分開來 。	there's nothing to separate the apple from the structure competition to the rival .
競爭對手和蘋果公司有同樣的能力製造所有這些產品 。	competitive opponents and apple companies have the same ability to make all of these products .
實際上 , 他們也嘗試過 。	in fact , they've tried .
幾年前 , 捷威公司推出了平板電視 。	a few years ago , agile company launched a tablet .
他們製造平板電視的能力很強 ,	they're very capable of making tv .
因為他們做平板顯示器已經很多年了 。	because they've been doing a flatboard display for years .
戴爾公司推出了mp3播放器和掌上電腦 , 他們產品的質量非常好 , 產品的設計也非常不錯 。 但是也沒有人買他們的這些產品 。	the company darre launched the mp3 players and the palms , and the mass of their product is very good , but nobody buys their products .

但是每天我們都這麼做 。	but we do it every day .

做公司的目標不是要跟所有需要你的產品的人做生意 ,	the aim of a company is not to do business with anybody who needs your product .
而是跟與你有著相同理念的人做生意 。	it's a business with people who have the same idea .
這是最精彩的部分 。 我說的這些沒有一個是我自己的觀點 。	this is the most amazing part . i mean , none of these are my own views .
這些觀點都能從生物學裡面找到根源 。	all of these perspectives can be found in biology .
不是心理學 , 是生物學 。	it's not psychology , it's biology .
當你俯視看大腦的橫截面 , 你會發現人類大腦實際上分成三個主要部分 , 而這三個主要部分和黃金圓環匹配得非常好 。	when you look at the crosssection of the brain , you'll see that the human brain is actually divided into three main parts , and these three main parts and golden circles are very good .
我們最新的腦部 , 管轄智力的腦部 , 或者說我們的大腦皮層 , 對應著 " 是什麼 " 這個圓環 。	our latest brain , jurisdictional brain , or our cortex , corresponds to what the circle is .
大腦皮層負責我們所有的理性和邏輯的思考和語言功能 。	the cortex is responsible for all of our rational and logical thinking and language function .
中間的兩個部分是我們的兩個邊腦 。 邊腦負責我們所有的情感 , 比如信任和忠誠 ,	the two parts in the middle are our two sides , and the brain is responsible for all of our emotions , like trust and loyalty .
也負責所有的行為和決策 , 但這部分沒有語言功能 。	it's also responsible for all behaviors and decisionmaking , but it doesn't have language function .
換句話說 , 當我們由外向內交流時 , 沒錯 , 人們可以理解大量的複雜資訊 , 比如特徵 , 優點 , 事實和圖表 。	in other words , when we communicate with an extrovert , yes , people can understand a lot of complex information , like features , facts and graphs .
但不足以激發行動 。	but not enough to inspire action .
當我們由內向外交流時 , 我們是在直接同控制行為的那一部分大腦對話 , 然後我們由人們理性地思考我們所說和做的事情 。	when we're directly controlling brain conversations directly , we're thinking about what we call and what we do .
這就是那些發自內心的決定的來源 。	this is where those decisions come from .
你知道 , 有時候你展示給一些人所有的資料圖表 , 他們會說 " 我知道這些資料和圖表是什麼意思 , 但就是感覺不對 。 "	you know , sometimes you show people all the data graphs , and they say , " i know what the data and the graph is , but it's just not right . "
為什麼我們會用這個動詞 , " 感覺 " 不對 ?	why do we use the verb , the feeling , not right ?

或者有些時候 , 你說聽從心的召喚 , 或者說聽從靈魂 。	or at some point , you hear a call from your heart , or from your soul .
我不想把這些觀念分解得太徹底 , 但心和靈魂都不是控制行為的部分 。	i don't want to divide these ideas too thoroughly , but the heart and soul aren't parts of controlling behavior .
所有這一切都發生在你的邊腦 , 控制決策行為而非語言的邊腦 。	all of this happens in your brain and control the brain of decisionmaking rather than language .
如果你自己都不知道你為什麼幹你所做的事情 , 而別人要對你的動機作出反應 , 那麼你怎麼可能贏得大家對你的支援 , 從你這裡購買東西 , 或者 , 更重要的 , 對你忠誠並且想成為你正在做的事情的一分子呢 ?	if you don't know why you're doing what you're doing , and people respond to your motivation , then how can you win people's support , buy things from you here , or , more importantly , loyalty to you and be part of what you're doing ?
再說一次 , 目標不僅僅是將你有的東西賣給需要它們的人 ; 而是將東西賣給跟你有共同信念的人 。	again , the goal is not just selling the things you have to the people who need them ; it's selling things to the people you share beliefs .
目標不僅僅是僱傭那些需要一份工作的人 ; 目標是僱傭那些同你有共同信念的人 。	the goal is not just to employ people who need a job ; the goal is to hire those who have shared beliefs .
你知道嗎 , 我總是說 , 如果你僱傭某人只是因為他能做這份工作 , 他們就只是為你開的工資而工作 , 但是如果你僱傭跟你有共同信念的人 , 他們會為你付出熱血 , 汗水和淚水 。	you know , i always say , if you hire someone just because he can do this work , they just work for you , but if you hire a common belief , they pay you blood , sweat and tears for you .
這一點 , 沒有比懷特兄弟的故事更恰當的例子了 。	there's no more appropriate example than the narrative of the white brothers .
大多數人都沒聽說過塞繆爾•蘭利這個人 。	most of you haven't heard of this guy samuel lanley .
20世紀初期 , 投入機動飛行器的熱情就像當今的網站熱 ,	in the early 20th century , the passion of the airplane airplane was like the website today .

我的意思是 , 即便是現在 , 你問別人 " 為什麼你的產品或者公司失敗了呢 ? "	i mean , even now , you ask people , " why is your product or your company failing ? "
人們總是用同樣的三個東西以同樣的排列順序來回答你 , 缺乏資金 , 用人不善 , 形勢不好 。	people always use the same three things to answer you in the same sequence , lack of funding , disadvantaged , unfortunately .
總是那三種理由 , 所以讓我們來逐個分析一下 。	it's always those three reasons , so let's go ahead and analyze it .

所以說 , 資金不是問題 。	so funding is not a problem .
他在哈佛大學工作過 , 也在史密森尼學會工作過 , 人脈極其廣泛 。 他認識當時最優秀的人才 。	he's worked at harvard university , and he's learned to work in smithsonia , and he's incredibly wide , and he knows the best people at the time .

人們買的不是你的產品 ; 而是你的信念 。	people buy not your products ; they're your beliefs .

創新的傳播有一個規律 , 如果你不知道這個規律 , 你一定了解這個概念 。	innovation spreads with a regulation , and if you don't know the regulation , you must understand this concept
我們的社會中 , 有2.5%的人是革新者 。	2 . 5 percent of our society are innovators .
13.5%的人是早期的少部分採納者 。	13 . 5 percent of people are early a few adopters .
接下來的34%是早期接受的大多數 , 然後是比較晚接受的大多數和最後行動的 。	the next 34 percent is the early majority , and then the majority of the acceptance of most and final actions later .
這部分最後行動的人買按鍵電話的唯一原因是因為他們再也買不到轉盤電話了 。	the only reason why this eventually activist buys the key phone is because they can't buy the transfer phone anymore .
雖然我們在不同的時候會處在這個曲線上不同的位置 , 但是創新的傳播規律告訴我們如果你想在大眾市場上獲得成功 , 或者要大眾接納一個點子 , 你得等到獲得15%-18%的市場接受度這個轉折點之後才行 。 那時之後市場才真正開啟 。	although we're in a different position on this curve , the innovation regulation tells us that if you want to get a success in the mass market , or a public including an idea , you have to wait until 15 to 18 percent of the market acceptance in that twist . and then the market really opens up .
我喜歡問公司: " 你的新生意怎麼樣呀 ? "	i like to ask companies , " what about your new business ? "

對 , 我們一般這樣形容他們 。	yeah , we generally describe them .

這就是問題的所在 , 就是這點間隙 , 你得把這個間隙給填上 , 正如傑弗裡穆爾所說的 , " 跨越鴻溝 " 。 因為早期的大多數不會嘗試新事物 , 除非有些人已經先嚐試過了 。	and that's what the problem is , it's this gap , and you have to fill this gap , as jeffrey mull said , " cross the gap , because the majority of the earlier wouldn't try something new unless some of you have tried it .
而這些人 , 創新者和早期的少數人 , 他們喜歡大膽的嘗試 。	and these people , innovators and early people , they like bold attempts .
他們更自然地憑直覺做事情 , 發自於他們的世界觀的直覺 , 而不僅僅是因為市場上有什麼樣的產品 。	they naturally do things intuitively , from their worldviews , not just because of the products on the market .
這是一批在iphone上市的頭幾天去排隊等六個小時來購買的人 , 而其實只要等一個星期你就可以隨便走進店裡從貨架上買到 。	this is a bunch of people in the first few days of the iphone , waiting for six hours to buy , and actually just waiting for a week to get into the shelf .
這是一批在平板電視剛推出時會花4萬美金買一臺的人 , 儘管當時的技術還不成熟 。	this is a bunch of people who spent 40 , 000 dollars on the tv pushing out , even though the technologies weren't ripe .
補充說一下 , 他們並不是因為技術的先進而買那些產品 , 而是為了他們自己 。	and to add , they don't buy those products for the advances of technology , but for themselves .

我再舉些著名的例子吧 , 證實創新傳播規律的一個失敗的例子和一個成功的例子 。	let me give you another famous example of the failure of innovation and a successful example of success .

自從推出蒂沃機頂盒以來 , 大概是八、九年前 , 直到今天 , 它們一直是市場上唯一的最高品質的產品 , 這沒有任何異議 。	it's about eight or nine years since the top of the tiwagen box , until today , they've been the single highest quality product on the market , and it's not a dissent .

因為你會發現 , 蒂沃公司新推出他們的產品時 , 他們只是告訴我們他們產品是什麼 ,	because what you find is that when tivo launched their products , they just told us what their product is .
他們說 " 我們的產品可以把電視節目暫停 , 跳過廣告 , 回放電視節目 , 還能記住你的觀看習慣 , 你甚至都不用刻意設定它 。 "	they said , " our product can pause the tv show and skip it back on a tv show and remember your viewing habits , and you don't even have to set it intentionally . "
挑剔的人們說: " 我們不相信你 ,	and the picky people say , " we don't believe you .

你在唬人 。 "	you're bullshit . "

人們買的不是你的產品 ; 人們買的是你的信念 。 你所做的僅僅只是你的信念的證明而已 。	people don't buy your product ; people buy your beliefs , and what you do is just your belief .
下面我給大家介紹一個成功的例子 。	here's an example of success .
1963年的夏天 , 25萬人聚集在華盛頓特區聆聽馬丁•路德•金博士的演講 。	in the summer of 1963 , 250 , 000 people gathered in washington , dc listening to dr . martin luther king .

怎麼會有25萬人參加呢 ?	how do you get 250 million people involved ?
而且 , 金博士不是美國唯一的偉大演說家 ,	and dr . king is not the only great speaker in the united states .
也不是美國唯一一位在民權法案實施前遭受歧視的人 。	it's not the only person in the united states who's been discriminated before the civil rights act .
實際上 , 他的一些想法甚至不正確 。	in fact , some of his ideas aren't even correct .

維基百科是靠每天數萬人的更新 , 數百萬人的提取資訊而建立的 。	wikipedia is built on tens of thousands of people every day , millions of people extracting information .
這完美的說明了沒有一個人能比共同思考更聰明 。	it's a perfect description that nobody can think smarter than coincidence .
沒有一個人 , 沒有一個聯盟 , 沒有一個國家 , 能有我們共同思考更睿智 。	no one , no one , no coalition , no one country , can think together .
維基百科的宣言很簡單:建立一個能人人自由共享所有知識的世界 。	the statement of wikipedia is simple: building a world where humans can share all the knowledge .
所以 , 我想說 , 透過結合國際 , 多部門 , 公私力量 , 戰略通訊在一起 , 在21世紀 , 我們能創造共同的安全 。	so i want to say , by combining international , multiple sectors , private power , strategic communications together , we can create a shared security in the 21st century .
非常感謝 。	thank you very much .
